dövrii düşorgosini aşkar ctmişdir. Uzun illor Azıx mağarasında aparılan 
qazıııtılar bu orazido ibtidai iusanların holo 2 milyon il ovvol 
moskunlaşdığını vo bıı düşorgoniıı düııyada oıı qodim insaıı moskonlorindon 
biri olduğunu siibut ctınişdir. Lakiıı, Qarabağın Ermoııislan torofiııdon işğalı 
hom Azıx diişorgosiniıı, hom do bölgodoki digor tarixi-arxcoloji abidoloriıı 
elmi araşdırılmasınm qarşısını alnıışdır. Azıx palcolit düşorgosiııi koşf 
edilmosinin 50 illivino lıosr olunmuş bcynolxalq clıni konfraıısııı noşr 
olunan bu toplusuııda honı Azıx dıişorgosi, cyııi zanıanda Qarabağın vo 
ümumiyyotlo Azorbaycanııı digor daş dövıii abidolori, lıomçinin bütövliikdo

revealed in Karabakh Paleolithic site in the cave Azvkh. Tlıc long-term ex- 
cavations carried in the Azykh eave proved that already 2 million years ago

the most ancient Paleolithic monuments of the world. Unfortunately, occu- 
pation of Karabakh by Armcnia has madc to rcscarch historic- 
archaeological monuments in tlıis territory, including thc Az^ kh cave im- 
possible. Articles on thc site of Azvkh and other Stone Agc monumcnts of

WAS HOMO GEORGICUS RUNNING AWAY?
Reflections on the find-situation at Dmanisi (Georgia)
1.8 millions ago, at the time of Dmanisi, humans were an in- 
tegral part of nature in a warm steppe environment. If, some- 
where, a fauna including Mammuthus meridionalis, Dicerorhinus 
etruscus etruscus, Equus stenonis, Cervus perrieri and a bovid 
similar to Dmanisisbos georgicus together with Megantereon 
megantereon, Homotherium crenatidens, Pachycrocuta perrieri, 
Ursus etruscus and Canis etruscus occurs, we can assume that 
Man was also present.
Such a steppe environment existed south of the Eurasian 
high mountain chains and was inhabited by our ancestors during 
by far the longest period of our history. Much later - and proba- 
bly linked with the control of fire - humans were able to occupy 
the temperate zones north of the mountains.
At Dmanisi humans and animals stayed close to water. The 
herbivores (elephants, rhinos, bovines, horses and deer) came to 
drink. The predators (sabre-toothed cats, hyaenas, bears, wolves) 
came to hunt the herbivores. This explains the many bones of 
herbivores.
But why were many bones of carnivores also found? Mostly 
they do not represent old individuals and it can be excluded that 
they died due to natural causes.
Man was also present because of the herbivores. It may be dis- 
cussed whether he hımself was a hunter or whether he benefıted from 
the camivores’ prey. Ever since humans owned stone tools, first of 
all flakes with sharp cutting edges which enabled the dismembering 
of animal bodies, meat was an essential part of their food.
Humans were thus present for the same reason as the camivores. 
But this does not explain why there are so many human bones. Most- 
ly the bones are from young and strong individuals and nothing indi- 
cates anatural death.
It therefore seems possible that there were fights between hu-
252
mans and carnivores conccming the division of prey. The small 
wolves (('anis etruscus) were not a serioııs dangcr. Bears (Ursııs 
etruscus) were also not the problem; at Dmanisi thcy are paıtly 
reprcscnted by old animals But thcre werc the sabrc-toothcd cats 
(Megantereon megantereon, Homotherium crenatidens) and thc 
hyaena (Pahycrocuta perrieri), predators which even likcd to kill 
humans as a welcome prey.
Such a scenaıio may explain the find situation at Dmaııisi. 
The bones of sabıe-toothed cats, especially the skull of a jııvenile 
Megantereon megantereon with attached cervical and thoıacic 
vertebrae, indicate that the caınivores did not always prevail. 
But hıımaıı bones aıe also numeroııs...
How dangerous wcrc humans at tlıis time? The stone artcfacts 
were not wcapons but primarily tools used to cut up animal bodics. 
Thc muscular strcngth of Homo georgicus surely could not impress 
sabrc-toothed cats und hyaenas. So we may suppose that humans 
alrcad> had woodcn weapons, pcrhaps alread> lanccs.
In any case, the sitııation at Dmanisi seems to pıove that 
hıımans did not turıı to flight when carnivores appeaı ed.

PLEISTOCENE ART OF GOBUSTAN
At present, four sites with rock carvings were fıxed on the terri- 
tory of Azerbaijan (fıg.l):
1. Big Gobustan, covering the territory of Beyukdash, Kichik- 
dash, Jingirdag, Shaxgaya and Shongar mountains.
2. Absheron peninsula;
3. Gemigaya Mountain, the highest point of Small Caucasus -  
Kapyjyk (Nakhchevan) alpine summer pastures;
4. The foot of Delidag Mountain of Kelbajar, south-eastem 
slope of Small Caucasus.
Pleistocene Art of Azerbaijan is represented only in Gobustan on 
Beyukdash and Kichikdash mountains in the “Gaya arasi”, ”Jeyran- 
lar”, ”Kaniza”, ”Ana-zaga” and “Okuzler” sites. Here images of 
women in profıle, early hunters and Upper Pleistocene fauna: au- 
rochs, gazelles and wild horses are represented on the walls of the 
caves.
At the period of the fırst settlement of Gobustan on the place of 
the present scorched semidesert drought-resisting open woodland 
vvith pistachio trees, hawthom, willow pear, juniper and pomegranate 
was stretching. Natural conditions in Upper Pleistocene were closer 
to forests of tugai type in a damper climate (gallery forests).Analysis 
of pattems of fossilized pollen taken out of the remains of the hearth 
in Ana-zaga cave of Beyukdash Mountain in Gobustan showed that 
oak and pine trees were once growing here [Rustamov Dj.,1994]. All 
these let us suppose existence of areas with oak-pine woods in the 
nearest vicinities of Gobustan and in the coastal strip of the Caspian 
Sea. Pine trees are still growing on Kichikdash Mountain near Ga- 
raatli sanctuary (fıg.2).
In Binagadi bituminous deposits of Upper Pleistocene age re- 
mains of arborescent juniper (Junipems polycarpos) were found, 
which indicates wide spread of juniper woods at that time. Willow 
pear (Pims salisifolia), shmb cherry (Pmnus microcarpa), pomegra-
257
nate (Prunus mıcrocarpa), honevsuckle (Lonıcera), elm tree, vine, 
found ın Bınagadı deposıts, have recently grown m Gobustan and 
some of these types can be met there even today.
In Upper Pleıstocene savannah landscape was developing. The 
revealed thick piece of wıld vine (Vitıs conf.sılvestns) ın Binagadi 
presupposes existence of riparian forest here [Petrov V.A.,1939].
In upper Quatemary period boundaries of freshwater Khvalin 
(now Caspian) Sea transgression reached Mingachevır w'ater storage. 
Sediments of the sea with freshwater fauna of mollusks wrere found 
even near the Urals and Kazan [Vereshagm N.K.].
On the slopes of Gobustan foothills grass vegetation of Grami- 
neae type [Gromov I.M., 1952] was predominatmg and today it can 
be met in some places with higher dampness m Gobustan. On Ki- 
chikdash Mountain in Gayaarasi site, even nut trees have grown until 
recently. However, a number of deer rock carvıngs indicate exıstence 
of well-developed tugai woods that were probably later destroyed by 
a man [Vereshagin N.K., 1959]. On the basıs of found remains of 
arborous vegetation in Upper Pleistocene in ıts mountainous part, 
anyway, savannah landscape developed but it was formed in other 
way rather than contemporary savannahs of Africa. These north sa- 
vannahs represented lightwoods, formed by the trees with' winter de- 
foliation [Petrov V.A.,1939].
Such was a common picture of Upper Pleıstocene landscape- 
geographical flora of Gobustan. General desertıfıcation of open land- 
scapes in connection wıth glacier regression affected degradation of 
landscape of north savannah, development of semi-steppe and semi- 
desert plants on its place and increase of salinity processes.
Rock art of Azerbaijan is graphıcally planed. Images are gıven as 
silhouette, continuous or contour images. The view and volume are 
absent. Ammals and birds are always depıcted on one sıde (Beyuk- 
dash Mountain, Ana-zaga cave). Correlatıon of fıgures among them- 
selves produces conventional impressıon - sometimes animals and 
birds are represented with reverse orientation to each other: with the 
head up or down, etc. Characteristic features of animals are vividly 
expressed at these plane and realıstıc ımages. These plane and realis- 
tıc images sometimes seem to be closer to Aungnacıan ımages, al-
258
though some coarseness ıs felt m them. (Stones JSr2 64, 65 upper ter- 
race of Beyukdash Mountain) [M.Otte, 2004; 2006] .
Beyukdash Mountain, “Kaniza” site.
We meet images of aurochs heads, early hunters and aurochs. It 
should be noted that here separate stones with petroglyphs. Besides, 
a great number of artifacts made of bone were found here (fig.3).
Beyukdash Mountain, “Ana-zaga” site.
Analysis of images shows that images of aurochs, women and 
early hunters predominate here. (fıg.4).
Beyukdash Mountain, “Okuzler” site .
Here, mating themes chiefly predominate: 2 aurochs, men and 
woman holding each other by hands, images of 2 goats. (fig.5).
Kichikdash Mountain, “Gaya aras'ı” site.
Special interest arouses the image of big fish, 4m. long and 23 
sm. wide, on stone of j\°5 of Kichikdash Mountain (fig.6). Judging 
from approximate data thıs ıs an image of dolphin, which is an ex- 
tinct animal in this region. Existence of dolphins in the Caspian Sea 
ıs dated to Upper Quatemary period. Besides, in confirmation of the 
previously mentioned, thıs picture was executed on the wall of early 
hunters’ cave, at the foot of which a cultural layer with Upper Paleo- 
lithic industıy was revealed. From this cultural layer nucleuses, tra- 
pezes, denticulate bladelets and bone punches possessing Upper Pa- 
leolithic image were found. In this site approximately 4 m. deep a 
separate stone with the sıgn image was found. (fig.7). So, the history 
of the origin of the givcn picture one can refer to the end of Upper 
Pleistocene period, w'hcn the last bıg transgression of the Caspian 
basin- Khvalin Sea took place. At that period the waters of the Medi- 
terranean Sea reached thc Caspian Sca through the Black Sea. i.e. vıa 
Manych Strait. In Khvalın layer Manych Strait was open in Vurme.
Kichikdash Mountain, “Jeyranlar”site
Vanous themcs represented on the walls of thıs sıte: ımages of 
gazelles, aurochs and women (fıg.8).
These data based on fiırther research and excavations in rock 
caves and at thc foot of some multilayeredly paınted rocks, allow us 
to reconsider the chronology of Gobustan. Until recentlv, the ques-
259
tıon about more ancıent origin of early monumcnts of Gobustan has 
been mainly a private, and not a pnncipal questıon.
Prelımmary publicatıon on problems of chronology had been al- 
ready made, but now it ıs more carefully studıed. As a result, totally 
new data on datmg of images were obtained, Today we possess 
some opportunities to give a full and rather concrete answer to the 
questıon of dating in the rock art of Azerbaıjan.
First work on penodization of rock carvmgs of Azcrbaijan was 
ımplemcnted by archaeologıst I. Jafarzade in 70-th of last century.
Petroglyphs of Gobustan, mvestıgated by him accordmg to their 
style, content and dating were dıvıded into 6 hıstoncal-chronological 
groups since the most ancient tımes until the perıod of thc Middle 
Ages:
1. The most ancient, early penod of Neolithıc- VIII millennia 
BC. Silhouette fıgures of men and w'omen in fullface and profıle with 
the bow on their shoulders represented in this period.
2. Late - Neolithic period -VII-IV millennia BC. Images of au- 
rochs, boats and small images of archers.
3. Later - Eneolıthıc period —IV-III millennia BC. The big fıg- 
ures of dears. goats and lions in profıle.
4. Bronze Age period -  III-II millennia BC. Imagcs of gazelles, 
horses, pigs, dogs and wild anımals.
5. Iron Age period -  II-I mıllenma BC. Imagcs of man, goats 
and dears in a small size and Roman inscription.
6. The period of the Mıddle Ages -VIII-IX centuries and later. 
Images of caravans of camels, riders armed by spcars. Signs, s}'m- 
bols, engraved mscriptıons by Arabic and Farsi alphabet.
After his follower Dj.Rustamov (Rustamov,2006. p.86-87) 
publıshed that fırst settlcrs -  early hunters appcared in Gobustan XV- 
XX thousand years before and the most ancient petroglvphs dated by 
the end of Upper Paleolithic -  beginnmg of Mctholithıc.
However, new data on datmg of petroglyphs, obtamed for today, 
requıre some specifıcation and modifıcation in chronology and peri- 
odizatıon made by l.Jafarzadc.

Archaeologıcal ınventory, revealcd ın thc sıtes and caves of Go- 
bustan is a valuable matcnal for thc solution of some problems of 
dating petroglyphs. Let us consıdcr one of them, basing on the divi- 
sion of westem and Russıan histonans.
Ana-zaga cave
Ana-zaga cave is situated on the upper terrace of Beyukdash 
Mountain in Gobustan. Since 1966 archaeological excavations had 
been held here. With the aim of establishment of absolute dating of 
Gobustan monuments samples from thc cultural layer at the depth of
1 m. 85 sm. were takcn for radıocarbon dating in Ana-zaga cave. 
From the given cultural layer archaeologists J.Rustamov and 
F.Muradova revcalcd choppers, coneshaped. pencilshaped and cylm- 
dric nucleuses ın 1977. The mventory of the site also consists of chı- 
sels, mıcroedges, kmfelıke plaıts. segmcnts, flint trapezıums, mıcro- 
plates, percussion tools made of river stone and w'eight stones. Hcre 
fragments of scparate stones with anthropomorph images were also 
found. (fıg.9).
As we sec petroglyphs arc to a lesser or greater degree connected 
with the archaeologıcal laycr. In such cases establıshment of the age 
may be absolutely precise. Consequently, these petroglyphs are older 
or of the same age wıth thc formatıon of the layer. Petroglyphs of 
Gobustan on the walls of Ana-zaga cavc (stones jVs 29, 32, 39) are 
fully ıdentıcal both on thcır style or techniques of executıon wıth 
separate stoncs with ımages, rcvcalcd from the archaeological layer.
In 2009 condııctcd research Ict us reconsidcr the question of dat- 
mg of Gobustan petrolyphs.
Common thickncss of thc cultural layer of the cave comprised 4
m.
Sample taken from the boncs and soıl wıth the ash takcn from 
thc mark from thc cultural laycr at the dcpth of 1 m. 85 sm. wcre 
dated wıth radiocarbon mcthod ın New Zealand. If the given petrog- 
iyphs on separatc stoncs wcre carlie: dated by archaeologısts back to 
thc VIII-VII B.C. primary calıbrated data showed 9029 B.C. lt 
should be noted that lowcr than the dated level thcre are cultural lay- 
crs on the levcl of 15sm, 95sm, 1.6-1.65 m, 1.75mn2.15m and thıs. 
in ıts tum, lets us datc thc lowest level of the sıte of the gıven cavc 
by the end of Upper Paleolith- early stagc of Mesolith. Consequcntl\.

petroglyphs vvıth analogous style and technıques of execution on 
separate stones may be dated back to thıs age. (fıg. 10,11).
The subject of special interest are small river stones wıth en- 
graved zigzag like pattems, revealed in Ana-zaga cave on the level o f
2 m. 85sm. -  3m (fıg. 12).
Ana-zaga cave is not the only place where archaeologıcal exca- 
vations were held. In Gobustan archaeologists revealed such ancient 
sites as «Firuz -1», «Gaya-arasi - 1», «Gaya-arasi - 2», «Kamza» 
and so on. In “Kanıza” site thickness of the cultural layer reached 5 
m. At present works on testmg and dating of these cultural layers 
have been going on.
Summary
Results of research let us consıder the chronology of Upper Pa- 
leolithic rock carvings in a little different way. On the whole, ıt looks 
like this:
I.The most ancient, early stage - the penod of Late Pleısto- 
cene and early Holocene period of aurochs.
II. This period, in its tum, is subdivided into four style groups:
I  style: the image of ox head in Gayaarasi site of Kichikdash 
Mountain, and also the image of the ox head on separate sto.nes of 
Okuzler-2, Kaniza sites of the upper terrace of Beyukdash Mountaın, 
stone N° 33 (45) of the upperterrace of Beyukdash Mountain.
II style: Images of oxen in full size, reverse bas-relief images of 
women (stone Jfe 65, 29 of the upper terrace of Bcyukdash Moun- 
tain).
III style: Images of oxen wıth short legs and stretched bodies, 
klaviform signs, sueh as on the upper terrace of Bcyukdash Moun- 
taın, stones JVe 29, 65.
IVstyle (X-VIIImln.B.C.): 1) Reverse bas-relıef images of men
- hunters and images of hunters wıth bows and arrows; 2) ımages on 
separate stones that were found from cultural layers of such settle- 
ments, as Okuzler-2 and Kanıza of the uppcr terrace of Beyukdash 
Mountain, Gayaarası site of Kichikdash and Shongar Mountaıns. 
Here, mainly, petroglyphs of hunters, women, oxen and shıps are 
presented.
So, for the fırst time petroglyphs of Gobustan are dated on the 
basis of dated archaeologıcal material. These fmdings charactcrize
262
stages of the end of Upper Paleolıth of Gobustan. They give us no- 
tion about development of culture of ancient Stone Age in the course 
of several millennıa. If in the previous editions artifacts of the cultur- 
al layer in Ana-zaga cave found 1 m. 85 sm. deep were dated back to 
the VIII-VII mln. B.C., now with the help of AMS dating quite new 
results were obtained: 9029 B.C. These data, in its, tum, let us offer 
more ancient dating of the earliest rock carvings of Gobustan. Stu- 
died materials also helpful in estimating the place of Paleolithic art in 
the context of the hıstoıy of Central Europe and Asia in a new way 
and reveal its importance. Though diffıculties in research and not 
full study and publıcatıon of the obtained material leave lots of con- 
siderable gaps, yet. Gobustan is not only the most ancient centre of 
rock art but also sui genens, a single monument in Azerbaijan and on 
the whole Caucasus. In its tum, some datıngs require additional 
substantiation.

THE LOWER Paleolithic INDUSTRIES 
OF NORTHERN ASIA
The earliest chronologıcal posıtion in the anthropogenıc history 
of Northem Asia occupied by the materials of the multilayered Ka- 
rama site m the northwestem Altai Mountams. Karama is located in 
the Anui River valley in 14 km downstream from the well-known 
archaeological site of Denisova Cave. Excavatıons were established 
at an elevation of 51 m above the river surface. The profıle exposed 
more than 11 m of Pleistocene deposits. The features of the sedi- 
ments of the Karama site allow for the establishment of three strati- 
graphic unıts with different depositional and structural characteris- 
tics. These three independent unıts are separated by long hiatuses in 
sediment deposition (Ulianov, Kulik, 2005; Zykin et al., 2005).
The upper part of the profile (strata 1-6) is composed of a loess- 
like loam with several horizons of buried soil. The lithological layers 
of the covering sub-aerial sediments are well correlated with the stra- 
tigraphic horizons of the Middle and Upper Pleistocene recognized 
within the loess-soil sequence of Westem Siberia. Conseqıiently, the 
period of formation strata 2-6 of the Karama sedıment corresponds 
to Oxygen Isotope Stages 2-9. Given the formation of this deposits 
corresponds to the Oxygen Isotope Stage 9, the age of the underlying 
red-colored deposits should exceed 340 ka BP.
The red sediments of the mıddle stratıgraphic unıt (stratum 7) 
are composed of poorly sorted, redeposited montmorillonite clay 
with an admixture of various-grained sand, gravel and a considerable 
amount of heavily weathered granite boulders. The northwestem Al- 
tai red sediments have been thoroughly studied at the Chemy Anui 
profıle, established 20 km upstream from Karama at an elevatıon of 
60 m above the modem river surface of the Anui valley. The profile 
revealed a sequence of intercalating reddish-brown clay and thin lay- 
ers of detritus embedded in yellow clay. Screemng of the yellow clay 
sediments yielded numerous mollusk shells. The taxonomic compo- 
sitıon of available shell ıs characteristic of the Lower and Early Mıd-
dle Pleistocene deposits of the southem part of Westem Siberia. A 
RTL-date of 643 ka BP has been generated on a sample from the yel- 
low clay layer with mollusk shells. Another date of 542 ka BP has 
been obtained for the overlying red sediments. The RTL dates are 
well correlated with the paleontological characteristics of the profıle 
and in general suggest the Early Middle Pleistocene age for these 
deposits.
Geological and geomorphological position of the red sediments 
of the Chemyi Anui profıle within the structure of the Anui valley, 
the period of the Chemyi Anui red sediments formation generally 
corresponds to the penod of accumulation of red sediments at the 
Karama profıle. Hence, the youngest age of the Karama site can be 
estimated to be the upper border of the Early Middle Pleistocene.
The lower portion of the Karama profıle (strata 8-14) demon- 
strates a sequence of alluvial sedimentary layers. The floodplain se- 
diments revealed two horizons of compact slitozem soil (strata 10). 
Compact buried soils are not typical of the Middle and Upper Pleis- 
tocene of North Asia. Thus, the occurrence of compact soil serves as 
indirect support for the carly age of this pedocomplex.
According to the palinological research results, it has been de- 
termined that the pollen spectra from the lower and middle parts of 
the section contain the signifıcant amount of the exotic elements of 
dendroflora (Bolikhovskaya, Derevianko, Shunkov, 2006). These 
include nemoral European and Far Eastem taxa -  heartleaf hom- 
beam, oriental hornbeam, hop hombeam, English oak, small-Ieaved 
lime, Amur limc, Manchurian lime, Chinese elm, mulberry-tree, 
which were for the fırst time recorded in the regional fossil flora. The 
presence of pollen of these plants and the environmental-coenotic 
features of the discovered taxa (Grichuk, 1982) allow to dctermıne 
the age of the enclosing deposits, vs'hich are no younger, than the ear- 
ly Middle Pleistocene). The results of the climate-stratıgraphic diffe- 
rentiation of the section and the obtained paleoclimatic reconstruc- 
tions point to the formation of these deposits during the four climati- 
cally different paleogeographic stages of the Eearly Middle Pleisto- 
cene. These four stages correspond to succession of the two warm 
and two cold penods of the interglacial and glacial classcs. In aggre- 
gate, the materials of the palinological analysis, along with other ana-
271
lytical data, make it possible to assume that accumuiation of these 
deposits corresponds to Oxvgen Isotope Stagcs 16-19. In other 
words, the age of the deposits can be descnbed by the tıme range 
between 600-800 ka BP.
The archeological materials of Karama are represented by the 
sets of stone artıfacts, characteristıc of the Lower Paleolithic indus- 
trics of the pebble type (Derevianko, Shunkov, 2005). Large, non- 
rounded fragments of volcanıc acıdıc rocks (predominantly the sphe- 
rulite effusives from the colluvial-proluvıal local deposits) seıved as 
raw material forthe tool production (Kulik, Shunkov, 2001). Accord- 
ing to the petrographic composition, the artifacts differ from the de- 
tritus from the enclosing deposits of the sectıon. This indicates deli- 
berate selection of raw materials for thc tool production. Tlıe raw 
materials were represented by fragments of volcanıc rocks of varia- 
ble sizes and quality. These rocks were comıng from the channel de- 
posits of the streams, which were carrying thc stone matenal from 
the watershed. The use of effusive rock can be cxplained by the pres- 
ence of this material in the stream channel, closest to the site. The 
effusıve material proved to bc more durablc, than thc rest of the 
available rocks.
Within the archaeological collection of the Karama, the primaıy 
rcduction products include corc-like flaked pebblcs with plain and 
roughly prepared striking platforms, a triangular corc with one flak- 
ıng surface and convcrgent flaked latcral sides, a plain striking plat- 
form and negative scars of parallel removals. as well as spalls wıth 
sub-parallel dorsal scar pattems and a plain or facetted strikmg plat- 
form. The major components of the typologıcallv dıstmct tool kit 
mclude racloırs of longıtudinal and transverse varietıcs. On thc ma- 
jority of specimens, thc thick cnd opposing the w'orking edgc bears 
either a natural or a ndged surface and w'as used as a back. Large 
pebble tools constıtute another characterıstic tool type of this ındus- 
try. This group includes choppers with straight. coııvcx and concave 
working cdges and massıve bases. Thc tools from thıs category is 
noteworthy. It ıs a “carcnated’' pebble tool with signs of steep reduc- 
tıon of the vvorkmg edge, producing a morphologv that ıs rcmmıscent 
of the so-called core-scrapers. which w'crc dcscrıbcd by M. Klein- 
dıenst (1961) ın tlıe Lower Paleolithıc ofEastem Africa. Pebble tools
272
wıth distinct spur-like protrusions or noses have been identified as 
typical Lower Paleolithıc tools. The tool kit of this assemblage in- 
cludes a point with a deep notch at the base fashioned on a large tri- 
angular spall, curved in profıle view and slightly asymmetrical from 
above, a “carenated” point with a massive, wide working element, a 
side-scraper with a ridged back, and a knife fashioned on a lamellar 
citron spall with a natural straight back and distinct signs of use-wear 
on the convex working edge. Also, there are denticulate, notched and 
simılar to them morphologicaliy beak-like tools fashioned on pebble 
spalls as well as spalls bearing signs of irregular retouch, including 
specimens with parallel dorsal scar pattems and prepared striking 
platforms.
At present, of the Karama culture-bearing layers represent the 
most ancient evidence of human occupation established in strati- 
graphic context in North Asıa.
In Tuva, the materials of Lower Paleolithic appearance are 
found at the locality of Torgalyk A (Astakhov, 1986, 1998). The par- 
ticular features of the geomorphological position and signifıcant cor- 
rasion of the stone tools allowed determination of at least the Middle 
Pleıstocene age of the site. Among the artifacts, affected by corrasion 
there are cores with elements of Levallois flaking and scrapers with 
longitudinal working edge, massive points and grattoirs, notched and 
denticulate tools. The specifıcs of this industıy is determined by pri- 
mitive bifaces, manufactured in the form of limands and proto- 
lımands and also the almond-shaped and oval bifacial tools.
In the Kuznetzk depression, is located the Lower Paleolithic ob- 
ject, known as thc MK-1 site (Dereviariko, Markin, 2007). Its tem- 
poral minımum, which is determined by applying the combination of 
bio-stratigraphic methods, refers to the initial boundary of the To- 
bolsk tıme (Oxygen Isotope Stages 9). The small collection of stone 
tools is charactenzed by fairly archaic appearance. At the same tıme, 
it includes artifacts with signs of parallel flaking.
In the Lower Paleolithic localities of the Middle Enisey region, 
the researchers describe series of the most archaıc artifacts, dcfıned 
among the corraded matenals of the Kurtak archeologıcal region ın 
the Minusinsk depressıon. The accumulations of corraded tools were 
found togethcr with remains of the mıddle Pleistocene fauna in the
273
zone of the offshore motion of sediments of thc Krasnoyarsk reser- 
voir, in the stratigraphic interval between the paleosoil of Kasantzev 
age (Oxygen Isotope Substage 5e) and the base of the Pliocene ter- 
race of the Enisey River (Drozdov, Chekha, Khazarts, 2005). Within 
the group of the Lower Paleolithic industnes the signs of two tech- 
nical traditions of stone raw material utılizatıon were noted (Droz- 
dov, Artemev, 1998). The materials of the Raslog II and Rasliv local- 
ities axe characterized by typical pebble character. Among the stone 
tools dominate radial and orthogonal cores, choppers and backed 
tools on citron-like flakes. Another tvpe of stone industry is 
represented by the materials from the Kamenny Log and Verkhni 
Kamen objects. These collections, along with large pebble tools and 
backed citron-like implements, include artifacts with morphological 
characteristics of Levallois and proto-prismatic flaking.
In the south of Middle Siberia, at the early stage of Paleolithic, 
the presence of corraded tools made of quartzite was noted in ex- 
posed beddings on high slope altitudes and on anthropogenic beaches 
along the right shore of the Angara River and also m relocated condi- 
tion at the base of Muruktin sediments (Oxygen Isotope Stages 4) 
(Medvedev, 1983; Medvedev, Vorob’eva, 1998). In accordance with 
the conditions of relative statigraphy and the degree of atmogenic 
corrasion of the surface, these artifacts must be dated no earlier than 
the Tazov time (Oxygen Isotope Stages 6). Among the archaic im- 
plements made of quartzite there have been distinguished oval cores 
with radial (centripetal) preparation of flaking surface, fan-like and 
parallel Levallois cores, side-scrapers, transversal and dejete-like 
scrapers, points and grattoris on massive flakes, choppers and chop- 
pings with straight and pointed working edge. All the localities in the 
Angara region are grouped into two large subdivisions, marked as 
Tarakhay and Olon complexes. Pebble tradıtions are clearly seen in 
the industries of the Tarakhay group. In the prımary flaking the ci- 
tron flaking technique was frequently used and various choppers 
were widely represented in the tools selectıon. The Olon variant ıs 
closer to the industries of the Acheulean type. The Olon tools are 
characterized by the presence of core-like ımplements with bifacial 
radial preparatıon and unique micro-bifaces made of quartzite, con- 
sidering the relatıvely small amount of pebble tools.
274
Thereby, the brief survey of Lower Paleolithic complexes of 
Northem Asia attests to the occupatıon of the region by a Homo 
erectus populatıon that invaded during the first human migration out 
of Africa (Derevıanko, 2005). According to the latest analytical data, 
based on the oldest Paleolithic fmds from the multilayered Karama 
site in the Altaı, the appearance of erectus in northem regions of 
Asia refers to the time period between 600-800 ka BP.

CORROBORATED HYPOTHESIS 
OF AZERBAIJANI SCHOLAR
The lower jaw of a primitive man was discovered in the course 
of excavation of a Lower Paleolithic site in Dmanisi, 85 kilometers 
of Tbilisi in 1991. That was the fırst finding of a series of anthropo- 
logic discovenes made at the Dmanisi Lower Pdeolithic site in 
South Georgia at later years. Currently, the Dmanisi anthropologic 
collection numbers more than 50 specimens including different 
bones of skeleton of hominids |JIop^KnnaHH^ae, BeKya, 2006]. The 
age of the Dmanisi Löwer Paleolithic site, which was identifıed as a 
result of Paleo-magnetic exploration of lava streams and isotopic 
dating of basalt lava under the cultural layers -  2.0 million to 1.8 
million years [HHopa^3e, 2000] -  was astonishing as well. Of para- 
mount importance in this series of anthropologic discoveries was that 
they were accompanied by pebble industry, which has much in 
common with handaxe-free stone industries identifıed in East Africa 
(Olduvai, Koobi-Fora, etc.) [HnopaA3e, 2006].
Materials about unique anthropologic and archeological disco- 
veries in Dmanisi were published in different scientifıc works. And 
more than 20 years before these events, in 1970, the scientifıc edition 
of the Medical Institute of Azerbaijan published an article by Azer- 
baijani scholars Mamedali Huseynov and Demir Gadjiyev devoted to 
the discovery at Cave Azykh two years earlier [Pafl>KHCB, ryceHHOB, 
1970].
The 1968, a team of archeologists involved in Paleolithic re- 
searches of the Institute of History of the Academy of Sciences of 
Azerbaijan that carned out excavations at Cave Azykh’s Middle 
Acheulian 5th layer undeı the lead of Mamedali Huseynov discovered 
a fragment of the jaw of a hominid who had lıved here 400,000 years 
ago. The jaw was investıgated by Paleo-anthropologist Demır Gad- 
jiyev and callcd Azykhantropus by the authors. That was the earliest 
fınding of a trace of fossil man in the post-Sovıet area.
Later excavations at Cave Azykh uncovered more ancıent lay-
277
ers; the site tumed to be the most ancıent one m the post-Soviet area 
and the world’s only site o f  cave where cultural layers in a single 
section cover a huge period of the primordial hıstory of mankind, 
ranging from the pebble culture to Moustenan | B c : ih h k o , et al. 
1980]. Complex (archeological, geological-geo-morphologic, Pa- 
leontologic, palynological, Paleo-magnetic, Paleo-geographical, etc.) 
studies carried out at Cave Azykh have identifıed that the Cave w a s  
inhabited by a man 1 million to 1 .2  million years a g o  and that the life 
continued within almost the entire duration of thıs period (raA>KKCB 
et al. 1979]. In terms of chronological range of ıts cultural layers, 
from the epoch of pebble culture (Olduvai) to the fırst half of the 
Mousterian inclusively (more than 1 million years), Azykh w a s  
ranked as a unique archeological monument [F e p a c n M O B  et al. 1981]. 
Today, Azykh continues to remain a unique site of cave of a primi- 
tive man where archeological layers cover a huge period of the pri- 
mordial history of mankind.
In his book titled “Azerbaijan’s Ancient Paleolithic” issued in 
1985, Mamedali Huseynov quite not groundlessly hypothesized that 
the Kuruchay Valley where Cave Azykh and the whole South Cauca- 
sus are situated had been inhabited by hominids long before the Cave 
was settled and even called the date: 2 million years [TyceHHOB, 
1985a].
TTıis hypothesis had all right to existence beeause another four 
archeological layers (layers VII-X) dating back to the Absheron 
epoch had been discovered under the Cave’s Layer VI (according to 
Paleo-magnetic method, the foot of Layer VI was dated back to the 
Brunes-Matuyama epoch, i.e. 780,000 years). The prevalence of 
pebble forms, the absence of axes, the coarseness and primitive na- 
ture of secondary processing techniques strongly differed the indus- 
try of Layers VII-X from the Early Acheulian Layer VI. The typo- 
logical composition of pebble tools distinguished from the most an- 
cient pebble cultures of Africa, Asia and Europe; with thıs in mind, 
Huseynov regarded the industry of Azykh’s lower (VII-X) Layers as 
a peculiar pebble culture he called “Kuruchay culture’ (in honor of 
the name of River where the site is situated) [F yceH H O B , 1979].
The cave was inhabited by hominids who had already had de- 
veloped skills of making tools. This is to conclude from the existence
278
of 17 stone artifacts of pebble eulture (dıscovered at Cave Azykh’s 
most ancient Layer X), whıch included choppers, chopping tools, 
protolimaces and flakes [Azərbaycan Arxeologıyası, I c., 2008]. 
With this in consideration, Huseynov thought Kuruchay inhabitants 
had acquired these skills long before the Cave was mhabited through 
settling open-end expanses of the Valley of River Kuruchay approx. 
1.5 million-2 million years ago [F y c e n H O B , 19856].
The discovery of the Lower Paleolithic site of Dmanisi in Geor- 
g ia  a n d  subsequently of Aınikab I and Muhkay I in Dagestan 
[A vm pxaH O B , 2007], was an indirect confirmation to Huseynov’s 
hypothesis that the regıon had been inhabited by hoıninids 2 million 
years a g o .  However, these were not the only confirmations.
The revision of the age of the terrace of River Kuruchay has al- 
lowed dating back the penod of thc Cave’s being mhabited by homı- 
nids to a much more ancıent period. Inıtıally, the date of the Cave’s 
being settled was tıed up to the 180 to 200-meter heıght above the 
terrace of River Kuruchay, i.e. the Cave’s bemg settled became poss- 
ible only after thıs terrace was formed 1.2 million years ago when 
River Kuruchay cut into the place lower than the Cave’s entranee 
and hence, the danger of the Cave’s being flooded dısappeared 
[razpKHeB et al. 1979].
Later researches thought the terraces of Mmor Caucasus rivers 
should be correlated with the Caspian Sea terraces having a large 
height, something that makes the age of the 180-200-meter-hıgh Rıv- 
er Kuruchay more ancient. According to the authors of the study, 
Cave Azykh's most ancient cultural layers with pebble culture date 
back to the period of 2.1 million to 2.4 mıllion years ago [ B c j i h c b , 
MaHcypoB, 1999).
Accordıng to Jafarov; scientifıc researches carrıcd out jointly 
with European scholars have allowed datmg back the period of for- 
mation of the Kuruchay culture to 2.5 mıllion years ago -  the exact 
period of Cave Azykh’s being settled by a primitıve man [Coforov, 
2007; Azərbaycan Arxeologıyası, I c., 2008].
The discovery made at Azykh more than 30 years ago and the 
discovenes m Dmanisı and Dagestan at the boundary of the 20‘"-2 ls' 
centuries are links of a single cham closely interconnected in the 
terms of either anthropogenic or migratıon processes.
279
The favorable natural-elimatie eonditions that have been kept in 
the South Caucasus over millions o f years and favored development 
o f  hominids, as w ell as the latest discoveries give all grounds to be- 
lieve that the hypothesis expressed by Azerbaijani scholar Mamedali 
Huseynov a quarter o f  century ago would be fmding its confırmation 
in flıture.
